(S.) <foreign lang="ar">طَعَنَانٌ</foreign> is of a measure of inf. ns. of verbs denoting that in which is prolongation and perseverance; and aptly applies to deviation from the right course. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">طَعَنَ إِلَى أُمِّهِ</foreign> is said of a child, meaning <hi rend="ital">He raised his head</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">thrust with it</hi>] <hi rend="ital">towards the breast of his mother.</hi> (L.)          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  And <foreign lang="ar">طَعَنَ فِى الدَّارِ</foreign>, said of a branch of a tree, (L, Msb,) means <hi rend="ital">It inclined into,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">against, the house, rising:</hi> (L:) or <hi rend="ital">it inclined towards the house, extending sideways.</hi> (Msb.)          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">طَعَنَتْ فِى الخِدْرِ</foreign>, said, in a trad., of any one of the Prophet's daughters, when demanded in marriage, as denoting her disapproval, means <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">She entered within the</hi>
